\DoxyCodeLine{1070   \textcolor{comment}{// The most common form of cons strings are degenerate unbalanced left-\/heavy}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1071   \textcolor{comment}{// binary trees (i.e. where `second` is a flat string and `first` another}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1072   \textcolor{comment}{// cons string). This form is created when building a string by appending}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1073   \textcolor{comment}{// repeatedly: `str = "{}a"{} + "{}b"{} + ... + "{}z"{};}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1074   \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1075   \textcolor{comment}{// To optimize for this, we flatten in reverse-\/DFS order, i.e. right-\/to-\/left.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1076   \textcolor{comment}{// This way, the stack never grows beyond size 1. Additionally, we elide the}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1077   \textcolor{comment}{// stack push for the element that will immediately be processed next.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1078   \textcolor{comment}{// Finally, the iterative algorithm is split into two physically separate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1079   \textcolor{comment}{// loops -\/ the first is optimized for cases when the cons tree contains only}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1080   \textcolor{comment}{// sequential one-\/byte strings. The second handles all other cases}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1081   \textcolor{comment}{// generically.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1082   \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1083   \textcolor{comment}{// Note this implementation is highly tuned. Please don't change anything}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1084   \textcolor{comment}{// without watching benchmark scores.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1085 }
